<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_39536eb7-2413-41cb-83b1-10469cc9c93d'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer8651479427112490152">Climbing to the top of the social ladder is hard—falling from it is even harder.  Regina Afton used to be a member of the Fearsome Fivesome, an all-girl clique both feared and revered by the students at Hallowell High... until vicious rumors about her—and her best friend's boyfriend—start going around.  Now Regina's been frozen out, and her ex-best friends are out for reve</span>
  <span id="freeText8651479427112490152" style="display:none">Climbing to the top of the social ladder is hard—falling from it is even harder.  Regina Afton used to be a member of the Fearsome Fivesome, an all-girl clique both feared and revered by the students at Hallowell High... until vicious rumors about her—and her best friend's boyfriend—start going around.  Now Regina's been frozen out, and her ex-best friends are out for revenge.  If Regina were guilty, it would be one thing, but the rumors are far from the terrifying truth, and the bullying is getting more intense by the day.  She takes solace in the company of Michael Hayden, a misfit with a tragic past whom she herself used to bully.  Friendship doesn't come easily for these onetime enemies, and as Regina works hard to make amends for her past, she realizes Michael could be <i>more</i> than just a friend...if threats from the Fearsome Foursome don't break them both first.<br /><br />Tensions grow and the abuse worsens, as the final days of senior year march toward an explosive conclusion in this dark new tale from the author of <i>Cracked Up To Be</i>.</span>

<a href="/questions/418800-why-did-she-he-write-this-book">Why did she/he write this book??????? Don&#39;t act like i&#39;m being mean just answer my question.</a>
</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/91779812-kamryn"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1547182453i/91779812._UX100_CR0,2,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/91779812-kamryn">kamryn</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Courtney Summers used to have such lovely blog posts on her old blog (I wish she'd kept them up!), and I remember her talking about the book in them. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Courtney Summers used to have such lovely blog posts on her old blog (I wish she'd kept them up!), and I remember her talking about the book in them. Basically, I think she wrote it because she was interested in how mean girls work. The scene where Regina finds the old batch of notes between her and her ex-friends was taken from Courtney's real life: she remembered some girls from her school as being mean and herself as not as bad, but one day she found some old notes between them and realized, nope, she had been just as bad. I also remember her talking about how, while she was writing the book, she had friends sending her articles about real-life bullying - the "meat in locker" thing was also (sadly) taken from real life. I think Courtney likes to explore tough topics in her writing and this is one of them - can a former mean girl be forgiven by her peers (and herself) and start over?<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>

<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1546228'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F6624871-some-girls-are">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/91779812-kamryn"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1547182453i/91779812._UX100_CR0,2,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/91779812-kamryn">kamryn</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Liz was never *in* the group in the first place; Liz was Regina's non-group friend. Regina was getting closer and closer with Liz, and Anna didn't wan<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Liz was never *in* the group in the first place; Liz was Regina's non-group friend. Regina was getting closer and closer with Liz, and Anna didn't want to lose Regina as a friend, so she decided Regina couldn't be friends with Liz. She was basically "destroying (what she saw as) the competition".<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1641119459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12178945900657614374">Someone please order my heart to be quiet. It <em>won’t </em>listen to me.<br/><br/><strong> </strong>I feel so tired. It’s like reading this book took all my strength and left me with a melancholic sentiment.<br/><br/>I shake it off.<br/><br/>There you go. I feel better already.<br/><br/>Liar. How can someone just go on with their lives after they’ve read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are' title='Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Some Girls Are</a> and not give it a second thought? It’s so impossible I can’t even imagine an alternative universe where such thing is fathomable.<br/><br/>Regina used to be a terror. But then she went to a party and An</span>
  <span id="freeText12178945900657614374" style="display:none">Someone please order my heart to be quiet. It <em>won’t </em>listen to me.<br /><br /><strong> </strong>I feel so tired. It’s like reading this book took all my strength and left me with a melancholic sentiment.<br /><br />I shake it off.<br /><br />There you go. I feel better already.<br /><br />Liar. How can someone just go on with their lives after they’ve read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are" title="Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Some Girls Are</a> and not give it a second thought? It’s so impossible I can’t even imagine an alternative universe where such thing is fathomable.<br /><br />Regina used to be a terror. But then she went to a party and Anna’s – the monster queen – boyfriend <strong>tried to rape her</strong>. Everyone thinks they had sex, and that they both wanted it.<br /><br />Wrong. Wrong. Wrong. Yet, no one believes Regina when she cries <strong>RAPE</strong>. Now, she has to deal with bullies at every corner of her school’s hallways.<br /><br />It’s a strange feeling to be in the body of a bully being bullied. We don’t know what to think of the character… Should we sympathize? Should we do our best to understand her or hope for her destruction instead?<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are" title="Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Some Girls Are</a> is reminiscent of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a>’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21853636.All_the_Rage" title="All the Rage by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Rage</a>. <strong>It explores the idea of telling the truth but having no one believe us. </strong>It’s not only frustrating but also gut-wrenchingly sad.<br /><br />This book takes some unexpected turns.<br /><br />Instead of standing there and taking all the hatred in, Regina acts. She revolts against her assailers. At one point, we even go as far as asking ourselves if Regina is any better than Anna, the one orchestrating the attacks.<br /><br />She’s a very flawed character. She challenges us into debating if she deserves what’s happening to her or not. <strong>I love how it raises plural ethical questions.</strong><br /><br /><strong> </strong>Talking about the book calms me. I just want to warn interested readers that it’s not for the faint of heart and that it will possibly make you cry.<br /><br />It’s a risk you’ll have to take.<br /><br />But it’s worth it.<br /><br />Because <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a><br /><br />never<br /><br />disappoints.<br /><br /><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/?a_aid=lolareviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">BD</a> | <a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12178945900657614374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_170484125" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170484125" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170484125?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170484125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8018119395425171444">I'll get the small amount of negative out of the way first. This book was faultless right up until the very last minute where I felt the ending was pulled together too quickly and just ended up being a weak conclusion to a deeply emotional and, at times, horrifying novel. It's the only bad thing I have to say about this book and I was still left feeling certain that I would read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3521484.Cracked_Up_to_Be' title='Cracked Up to Be by Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cracked Up to Be</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8470445.Fall_for_Anything' title='Fall for Anything by Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fall for Anything</a>.<br/><br/>The story reminded me a lot of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/439288.Speak' title='Speak by Laurie Halse Anderson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Speak</a>. Both novels were extremely well-written w</span>
  <span id="freeText8018119395425171444" style="display:none">I'll get the small amount of negative out of the way first. This book was faultless right up until the very last minute where I felt the ending was pulled together too quickly and just ended up being a weak conclusion to a deeply emotional and, at times, horrifying novel. It's the only bad thing I have to say about this book and I was still left feeling certain that I would read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3521484.Cracked_Up_to_Be" title="Cracked Up to Be by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Cracked Up to Be</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8470445.Fall_for_Anything" title="Fall for Anything by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Fall for Anything</a>.<br /><br />The story reminded me a lot of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/439288.Speak" title="Speak by Laurie Halse Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Speak</a>. Both novels were extremely well-written with characters you could relate to and believe in; and they also both dealt with false accusations and the ostracisation of a girl by her friends and high school classmates. What was different was that where the protagonist of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/439288.Speak" title="Speak by Laurie Halse Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Speak</a> was largely ignored, Regina from this book was completely destroyed by a series of horrendous physical and mental attacks by those she had previously considered friends.<br /><br />It was a much more dramatic story than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/439288.Speak" title="Speak by Laurie Halse Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">Speak</a>. I was unable to stop reading; I cared so deeply about Regina and what the outcome of all this bullying would be for her. I also adored Michael. I didn't foresee him becoming such a lovable character but he continually surprised me.<br /><br />I don't know whether this book is a particularly accurate representation of relationships and fall-outs in high school... I had some awful experiences with bullying but I can honestly say I don't ever recall there being anything of this calibre. Then again, maybe I chose not to see this kind of thing. Either way, the book was so full of raw emotion and sadness and forgiveness. It's about the importance of learning to say sorry. Don't mistake this for another cheesy high school drama - it is so so much more!<br /><br /><a href="http://emilymay.me" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>

<div id="review_1224176016" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1224176016" />
    <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister"><img alt="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486056026p2/4971692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1224176016?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister">Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1224176016" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10895244318491155448"><b>*5 Stars*<br/><br/>I need a Tum.</b><br/><br/>Because that was some <i>serious</i> high school insanity.<br/><br/>Some Girls Are…<i>mean</i>, and genuinely effed up—and this story is a solid testament to that. But it’s also a very realistic portrayal of the ugly side of high school, and, more specifically, the vicious cycle of bullying. <br/><br/>I’m gonna go ahead and <b>five-star</b> this book for the simple reason that I could NOT put it down. The GENIUS writing style is what made this one shine, for me: compelling and raw, edgy and intense--I swallowed it</span>
  <span id="freeText10895244318491155448" style="display:none"><b>*5 Stars*<br><br>I need a Tum.</b><br><br>Because that was some <i>serious</i> high school insanity.<br><br>Some Girls Are…<i>mean</i>, and genuinely effed up—and this story is a solid testament to that. But it’s also a very realistic portrayal of the ugly side of high school, and, more specifically, the vicious cycle of bullying. <br><br>I’m gonna go ahead and <b>five-star</b> this book for the simple reason that I could NOT put it down. The GENIUS writing style is what made this one shine, for me: compelling and raw, edgy and intense--I swallowed it up whole. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Hallowell High: You're either someone or your not. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Meet <b>Regina:</b> A popular high school senior whose social status entirely plummets after only a single party. Regina goes from bully to <i>bullied</i> overnight, as she finds herself walking the footsteps of those she’s hurt in the past…<br><br><b>And it’s a living nightmare. </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395353505ra/8984387.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Regina’s pain was so palpable, I could literally <i>taste</i> the bitterness that was spewed upon her, and feel the sharp sting of rejection from her peers. Her character was flawed, and there were many times I didn't like her. <br><br>But she was also afraid … so afraid, she allowed the opinions of others to define her. <br><br>I really felt for Regina, and I appreciated the fact that her character didn't improve within a chapter or two, but instead evolved at a slow, believable pace. I still wouldn't say she’s “cured” from all her demons, and that’s what brought this story to life … the fact that its occurrences mimicked “life”, and tended to stray from the typical fictional YA-formula. <br><br>It’s not very often an author can throw out terms such as <i>
  <b>“we’re the kind of popular that makes our peers unable to sleep at night”</b>
</i>, and not elicit a dramatic eye roll...<br><br>BUT, this story is written in such a way where you can tell the author <i>gets</i> it. She knows how ridiculous and dangerous this behavior is, and yet she makes no excuses. She’s not afraid to embarrass her heroine; not hesitant to put her in the wrong. It never felt like we were getting a “prettied” up version for the sake of a morally-sound story. We don’t have to admire this narrator, but we’re damn sure gonna get a realistic portrayal of her shortcomings…and I really <b>
  <i>loved</i>
</b> that. <br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>He came here quiet — not shy, but removed, above it all. Like he just didn't care about us. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>The romance in this story is gentle and young, but its value touched me. <b>Michael</b> is a lonely outcast who has been thoroughly drenched in false accusations. He hates the girl who sparked these lies—Regina. But as these two form an unlikely relationship, Regina finds there’s a lot to learn about herself in the process. <br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>In high school, you don’t get to change. You only get to walk variations of the same lines everyone has already drawn for you. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>I can see why some readers may have been left unsatisfied with this story’s ending, but I thought it was perfect! I’m a strong believer in less-is-more, and I find that an overkill ending tends to weaken the story’s power. <br><br>In this case, I was given enough finality to feel the story was complete, but was still left to wonder about the characters a little--and that’s what keeps me in their world. <br><br><b>A captivating read!</b><br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2mh7uop" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="50" width="50" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347313i/701667.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><b>
  <u>Book Stats:</u>
</b><br><b>▪  Genre/Category:</b> Young Adult<br><b>▪ Romance:</b> Young, complicated love<br><b>▪  Characters:</b> Came to life. Flawed and unpredictable. <br><b>▪  Plot:</b> Bully turns to *bullied* overnight and experiences a harsh reality. <br><b>▪ Writing:</b> Phenomenal. Polished. Realistic dialogue. <br><b>▪ POV:</b> 1st Person: Heroine <br><b>▪  Cliffhanger:</b> None. Standalone<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10895244318491155448" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_82807428" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82807428" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82807428?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      Emily May
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82807428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6121254718254275996">As seen on <a href='http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/02/some-girls-are-by-courtney-summers.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Readventurer</a><br/><br/>What a mean, ugly, venomous, relentlessly cruel book this is! I almost developed some ulcer myself just by being in the main character's head. <br/><br/>The "mean girls" novels are not something that interests me very much in YA lit. Ever since <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6482837.Before_I_Fall' title='Before I Fall by Lauren Oliver' rel='nofollow noopener'>Before I Fall</a> I feel mildly dissatisfied in how such stories generally unfold. In <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6482837.Before_I_Fall' title='Before I Fall by Lauren Oliver' rel='nofollow noopener'>Before I Fall</a>, for instance, I thought there was a lot of humanizing and excusing of mean girls going on, with not enough of owning up to their actions and </span>
  <span id="freeText6121254718254275996" style="display:none">As seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/02/some-girls-are-by-courtney-summers.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a><br /><br />What a mean, ugly, venomous, relentlessly cruel book this is! I almost developed some ulcer myself just by being in the main character's head. <br /><br />The "mean girls" novels are not something that interests me very much in YA lit. Ever since <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6482837.Before_I_Fall" title="Before I Fall by Lauren Oliver" rel="nofollow noopener">Before I Fall</a> I feel mildly dissatisfied in how such stories generally unfold. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6482837.Before_I_Fall" title="Before I Fall by Lauren Oliver" rel="nofollow noopener">Before I Fall</a>, for instance, I thought there was a lot of humanizing and excusing of mean girls going on, with not enough of owning up to their actions and atoning. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are" title="Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Some Girls Are</a> is more pleasing in that respect. <br /><br />Regina, one of the school's meanest mean girls, ends up to be the target of her friends' (or frenemies') wrath and finally tastes her own medicine. The treatment of her is vile, but hey, who cares, she was distributing the same sort of punishments just a few days ago. She deserves everything that's coming her way, right?<br /><br />Hm, maybe. I won't lie, seeing an ex-mean girl suffer was pretty awesome. At first. But once you get to know Regina a little better, you can't help to feel horrified for her. And it's not only about the abuse (the beatings, humiliation, almost rapes) - she gives back almost as much of it as she takes. It's more about her inner world. Her mind, constantly fixated on fighting back, on guilt, on memories of being a part of a group of so-called friends who can squash you in minutes, on pressures of always hating and being hated. It's an awful way to think. It's a damaging way to live. <br /><br />I can't say I enjoyed this novel. You can't enjoy a punch to your gut that this book is. But I did appreciate it. I appreciated that this novel doesn't make excuses for Regina and forces readers to forgive her. There are some things in life that can't be easily forgotten and fixed with an <i>I am sorry</i>. But something more important happens here - a mean girl breaks out of the circle of hate and violence and maybe becomes a slightly more aware person. She has to continue carrying the burden of her past actions though. No easy fixes here. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6121254718254275996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_367091272" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/367091272" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/367091272?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=girls-gone-wild">girls-gone-wild</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=upstairs-neighbors">upstairs-neighbors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=readventurer-made-me-do-it">readventurer-made-me-do-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer367091272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2865272956489349442"><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rDFbsAZsm0Y' rel='nofollow noopener'>some folks...</a><br/><br/>this was my first book for <a href='http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/category/she%20made%20me%20do%20it/1.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>the readventurer challenge.</a> this was catie's recommendation for me, and i really liked it - yay! i had just finished reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12043771.This_is_Not_a_Test__This_is_Not_a_Test___1_' title='This is Not a Test (This is Not a Test, #1) by Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>This is Not a Test</a>, so i was glad to read another book by this author, even though this was more of a realistic YA book, and i tend to skew to the dystopian/horror side of the YA field.<br/><br/>this book is about a girl named regina who is nearly raped by her best friend/queen bee anna's boyfriend at a party. they are both part of a super-tox</span>
  <span id="freeText2865272956489349442" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=rDFbsAZsm0Y" rel="nofollow noopener">some folks...</a><br><br>this was my first book for <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/category/she%20made%20me%20do%20it/1.html" rel="nofollow noopener">the readventurer challenge.</a> this was catie's recommendation for me, and i really liked it - yay! i had just finished reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12043771.This_is_Not_a_Test__This_is_Not_a_Test___1_" title="This is Not a Test (This is Not a Test, #1) by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">This is Not a Test</a>, so i was glad to read another book by this author, even though this was more of a realistic YA book, and i tend to skew to the dystopian/horror side of the YA field.<br><br>this book is about a girl named regina who is nearly raped by her best friend/queen bee anna's boyfriend at a party. they are both part of a super-toxic clique at the school, untouchably popular, who go out of their way to destroy the lives of others. because anna is so unstable, regina does not mention the assault, but rumors get out, and she finds herself ostracized and forced into a climate of bullying and intimidation tactics that would do credit to a dictator of a small country. <br><br>bullying is still a serious problem in the high school environment (and here on goodreads - come on girls - you should love <i>every</i> book unconditionally! think of teh authors!!) and this is one of those important books that show that no one is immune to the terror that bored and clever teenage girls can inflict. <br><br>it is not a <i>fun</i> read, there will be plenty of wincing, but is a really good book to slap into the hands of a teenager. actions have consequences. maybe not right away, but teen girls are fickle, and anyone can be made a target at any point. <br><br>these are the hard-partying kids; <i>Jeanette lurches up from out of nowhere looking like a guaranteed good time. Strung out. I can never tell when she's over the party; the party's usually all over her.</i> some people have pointed out that their behavior stretches belief, but i disagree. this sounds exactly like the parties of my high school experience, even though i went to very few. i didn't drink and i didn't drive, and i preferred hosting smaller, more intimate, ummm plant-based gatherings in the safety of my own home, where i could control the atmosphere and the music and could be the good hostess with the making of english-muffin pizzas and whatnot. no one ever threw up at one of my parties. this makes me either a successful or grossly unsuccessful hostess, depending on your priorities.but these kids are drinking heavily and popping pills, and coming out of their haze just long enough to torture each other with the dirt they have acquired , or fabricated, on each other.<br><br>the only thing i didn't like were the seeming inconsistencies of regina's character. i mean, i know that that age is a period of transitions, <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=AZ1MdRgU7Hw" rel="nofollow noopener">i'm a boy and i'm a man</a> (yeah, i can quote pre-1980 alice cooper lyrics until the cows come home - try me) but it still bothered me. while i understand how a young girl could be lured into the popular crowd, and once there, could be compelled to perform acts of cruelty with the mob mentality and all that, it is the rest of it that bothers me. she seems to have two sides to her: the side that is incredibly scared and passive, and just takes her punishment, and the side of her that rebels and lashes out with all the creative cruelty she has learned at the hands of anna, who is a true redheaded sociopath. and she wobbles between these two impulses, which makes her character unpredictable, and therefore difficult to sympathize with or get behind. her latent violence is pretty terrifying - this girl could snap at any second. <br><br>a quick psa that will probably come back to haunt me: what happened to her at the party, the thing that set off the chain of events, was bad, but not the worst. a little self-defense? maybe carry a knife? a knife you know how to use - don't go into this all fumbly. all i know is that a knife saved me from a similar situation when i was 17.just - be smart, ladies. no one's going to come to your rescue except you.<br><br>things that strain my belief:<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br>1) really? anna slept through all of that?? you would think a girl so careful of guarding her alpha reputation would never get that wasted - too wasted to lose control which shows a weakness a character like her never would.<br><br>2) if you have the bruises, show the bruises. show everyone. the way she caves in the bathroom because anna is pissed is weird. it isn't just anna. there were the lesser-members of the group: marta, jeanette, bruce, henry. and josh. especially josh. what good is a boyfriend if he can't be counted on to kick the ass of the dude that tried to rape you? i understand that regina thought anna would be pissed if she thought she had slept with donnie, but those bruises and a torn skirt do not look like consensual sex. regina seems to have this convenient-for-the-narrative disappearing and reappearing backbone. you walk off in the middle of telling your (ex)boyfriend because he takes a phone call? it's rude, yeah, but say your piece, girl! it is frustrating for the reader. <br><br>3) out of the whole school, there are only two neutral people? the ih8ra page is joined by the whole freaking school. i get that these girls are virulent monsters that have ruined lives, and once one falls from the nest, it is open season, but <i>no one</i> else but liz and michael are above the high school nonsense? <br><br>4) was donnie trying again to rape her in that supply closet? seriously? that's insane.<br><br>5) why does michael stay around? especially after his disgust at her after the yourspace page incident, when he can see that she is totally getting off on her own petty revenge? not attractive, regina... i understand why she is proud of it - fighting back feels good, but <i>michael</i> doesn't, so his devotion feels weird. and she read his journal! right there in public! regina is kind of a shit that it is hard to root for.<br><br>6) so much hiding out! if you are not going to go to class, why hide out at the school? that is where people are shoving you down the stairs! get out of that building! i understand that <i>if i'm not moving, nothing bad is happening,</i> but go not-move somewhere else! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>so, i know all that sounds like i didn't like it, but they are just things that made me a little angry reading this book. but this book <i>should</i> make you angry. bullying is stupid. my high school was too small to really contain this kind of thing, so whenever i read about it, it is like a foreign country to me. but it happens. a lot. and it is truly stupid. stop bullying, dummies! <br><br>the end.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="2865272956489349442" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2006730325?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer317692657925810830"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers' title='Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Courtney Summers</a> sure doesn’t waste her time. When she writes stories, she means business and she’s all about the serious dirty business, I’m telling you. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are' title='Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Some Girls Are</a> for me is her darkest, grittiest novel yet, even scarier than her zombie duology. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are' title='Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers' rel='nofollow noopener'>Some Girls Are</a> is a story of girl who was once a part of the “Fearsome Fivesome” composed of girls who are so mean and so effed up, they scared the crap out of me. I couldn’t imagine what it would be like in the shoes of Regina who gets kicked out </span>
  <span id="freeText317692657925810830" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a> sure doesn’t waste her time. When she writes stories, she means business and she’s all about the serious dirty business, I’m telling you. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are" title="Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Some Girls Are</a> for me is her darkest, grittiest novel yet, even scarier than her zombie duology. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6624871.Some_Girls_Are" title="Some Girls Are by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Some Girls Are</a> is a story of girl who was once a part of the “Fearsome Fivesome” composed of girls who are so mean and so effed up, they scared the crap out of me. I couldn’t imagine what it would be like in the shoes of Regina who gets kicked out of this elite group because of a horrible experience twisted and manipulated into something untrue. Now the bully becomes the bullied as Regina now becomes the main subject of the school’s elite gang’s evil schemes. <br /><br />My heart was beating so hard from page one because despite Regina’s flawed character, she still earned my empathy and I was worried for her every day she went to school. I was cheering for her on her attempts to retaliate and many times I felt this twisted and creepy sort of satisfaction when she gets even.<br /><br />I’m just not too happy about the ending. I’m sure the author is simply trying to keep it real and I get that stories like this don’t end in happily ever afters but I just wish there were better resolutions on the gazillion conflicts in the story but specifically on this very serious issue which I thought wasn’t very well addressed. But l guess the story is just trying to align its conclusion to the main theme of the story. Some girls are mean, some girls are effed up and some girls are practically evil, nothing one can do about it. *sighs*</span>

<div id="review_1904253625" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1904253625" />
    <a title="Deanna " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15662887-deanna"><img alt="Deanna " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437589889p2/15662887.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1904253625?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deanna " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deanna " href="/user/show/15662887-deanna">Deanna </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1904253625" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer168171948939645490">2.5 Stars!<br/><br/>I came across this book the other day while browsing Audible. The description caught my eye and before I knew it, I had pressed that button and it was ready to go.<br/><br/>I was pulled in immediately. From the description, I knew it was going to involve a lot of bullying, but I don’t think I realized just how much it would affect me. <br/><br/>Regina Afton was once a part of the “Fearsome Fivesome”. However, an incident at a high school party changes everything for Regina. At school the following Monday </span>
  <span id="freeText168171948939645490" style="display:none">2.5 Stars!<br /><br />I came across this book the other day while browsing Audible. The description caught my eye and before I knew it, I had pressed that button and it was ready to go.<br /><br />I was pulled in immediately. From the description, I knew it was going to involve a lot of bullying, but I don’t think I realized just how much it would affect me. <br /><br />Regina Afton was once a part of the “Fearsome Fivesome”. However, an incident at a high school party changes everything for Regina. At school the following Monday morning not only is she shunned from the group, she becomes the sole target of their hatred along with some of the other students. Students Regina herself hadn’t been very kind too. In fact, she’d been downright vicious to some of them. She tries to explain herself but no one will listen and the bullying goes from bad to worse. Some people think she is finally getting what she deserves.<br /><br />This was one of the first times I used “chipmunk speed” as what was happening was really starting to get to me but I couldn’t stop listening. I would love to think these things don't happen but I know this stuff goes on….so I stuck it out. I’ve read some pretty violent books over the years and it’s not like this one was extremely violent (although there were a few difficult scenes) but the emotional torment was just so hard to take... it was brutal. I really didn’t feel like there was any downtime… time to come up for air.<br /><br />The book definitely kept me engaged. I’m trying not to give anything away so I apologize for being vague, but it was very overwhelming for me. However, there was no way I was going to stop reading... I HAD to know how things would play out. And then after another really intense scene …it just ends. Which in one way I think is good because not everything in life is wrapped up in a pretty bow. But on the other hand, it was just like…. that’s it?<br /><br />The book is well-written and I do see what the author was trying to get across… and there can never be too much awareness of these issues. However, for me, it was so overwhelming. But I’ve seen many positive reviews from readers who thought it was a great read…so I think it’s a case of “it’s not you, it’s me”.</span>
  <a data-text-id="168171948939645490" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_272411613" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/272411613" />
    <a title="Reynje" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje"><img alt="Reynje" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473722441p2/5590906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/272411613?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reynje" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reynje" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje">Reynje</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer272411613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17411543725864137551">I thought this book was going to burn a hole in my stomach.<br/><br/>Even now, when I think about it I feel a visceral surge of anxiety; it triggers a physical response that echoes the rapid heartbeat and shortness of breath that accompanied the reading.<br/><br/>I mean this as a compliment to Summers’ writing. The ability to elicit such an intense and provocative reaction is, I think, testament to her skill. Some Girls Are is almost relentlessly harrowing in its portrayal of bullying and abuse, accentuated by Regi</span>
  <span id="freeText17411543725864137551" style="display:none">I thought this book was going to burn a hole in my stomach.<br /><br />Even now, when I think about it I feel a visceral surge of anxiety; it triggers a physical response that echoes the rapid heartbeat and shortness of breath that accompanied the reading.<br /><br />I mean this as a compliment to Summers’ writing. The ability to elicit such an intense and provocative reaction is, I think, testament to her skill. Some Girls Are is almost relentlessly harrowing in its portrayal of bullying and abuse, accentuated by Regina’s acerbic voice and Summers’ razor-sharp instinct for pacing and dialogue.<br /><br />This is an unsettling and compelling story. The tension escalates rapidly as the stakes increase, and the novel (literally) doesn’t pull punches – to the point when beginning each chapter was accompanied by a mental flinch. It’s not always easy to read, but it is hard to put down.<br /><br />What delineates Some Girls Are from other novels I’ve read about high school bullying is the perspective. Through Regina, we experience the viewpoint of someone who is both victim and perpetrator, someone who is subjected to physical and psychological bullying, and also inflicts it. Taking this further, not only does Regina exhibit mean girl tendencies, but a part of her relishes them. Even as she becomes fully cognizant of how far-reaching and destructive her actions are, she is also aware that on another level, she takes a vicious pleasure in enacting them.<br /><br />This is an uncomfortable position to be in as a reader. It would be easy to categorise all who carry out this kind of torment as morally reprehensible villains. But Some Girls Are muddies this idea by examining the complex cycle of manipulation and abuse of power amongst the characters. The lines here are not clearly drawn; not all of those culpable are devoid of sympathetic – or at least, understandable – elements. Some Girls Are goes some way to explaining how such a deeply messed up dynamic is perpetuated – feeding off insecurity and intimidation, cultivated to exert control – without attempting to justify it. I don’t believe the novel asks us to defend Regina, but to acknowledge that these situations are rarely black and white. We’re not asked to excuse her actions, but to consider the context of them, to recognise how guilt, abuse and emotionally damaging relationships impact the way she responds to threatening situations.<br /><br />As such, Some Girls Are challenges the common perception of the high school ‘mean girl’ – often presented as little more than a caricature of evil – with a confronting level of physical and emotional cruelty entangled with “friendship” and the ever-shifting hierarchy within cliques. To deny that girls are capable of this kind of behaviour does a disservice to those who have experienced it, and for that reason I believe this is a brave novel, insisting that we face a disturbing reality.<br /><br />Considering the circumstances, buying into Michael’s ability to accept Regina is a big ask of readers, and I understand why some would struggle with how this particular plot line develops. I’m okay with this element of the story – in addition to fuelling the conflict in the final chapters of the novel I think it provides an interesting counter-balance to Kara’s consuming hatred and inability to let go. (And maybe I’m naïve but I want to believe that people are as capable of forgiveness as they are of torture).<br /><br />I feel that the ending is left largely open to interpretation. Personally, I don’t see this as the end of Regina’s story, but rather as the beginning of long, hard road. We don’t know what choices she will make once she leaves those stairs. Even the weaving together of hands is a tentative, fragile thing. A sliver of hope, not a life-preserver thrown into the sea of carnage. Summers offers a reprieve from the harrowing climax in suggesting that Regina has options, a chance to alter her course. But she doesn’t explicitly spell out what lies beyond the final page.. that is left up to you.<br /><br />I'm pretty sure <i>I</i> need an antacid right now. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17411543725864137551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_142301153" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/142301153" />
    <a title="Flannery" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/652877-flannery"><img alt="Flannery" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312843258p2/652877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/142301153?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Flannery" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Flannery" href="/user/show/652877-flannery">Flannery</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who like gritty YA</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=kcls">kcls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=young-adult-teen">young-adult-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=reviewed-2011">reviewed-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer142301153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16393977960758847457">Some girls are...<a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[total bitches <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. That's the takeaway from this book. High school is a nightmare for a large number of people and there will always be that crowd of people that finds pleasure in ruining the reputations of others. This book is like watching a trainwreck--it is completely awful, but you just have to keep reading to see how it all turns out. <br/><br/>Regina Afton was second in command to Anna, her best friend and head of the mean girls clique at Hallowell High S</span>
  <span id="freeText16393977960758847457" style="display:none">Some girls are...<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[total bitches <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. That's the takeaway from this book. High school is a nightmare for a large number of people and there will always be that crowd of people that finds pleasure in ruining the reputations of others. This book is like watching a trainwreck--it is completely awful, but you just have to keep reading to see how it all turns out. <br /><br />Regina Afton was second in command to Anna, her best friend and head of the mean girls clique at Hallowell High School. After an unfortunate event at a party involving Regina and Anna's boyfriend, Anna shuns Regina and turns the entire school against her. Cue 200 pages of torment. The only person (honestly, the only person) who even gives Regina a sliver of the light of day is Michael, a boy whose reputation she and her friends ruined a year or two earlier. (and we don't even know what his motives for speaking to Regina are for a large portion of the book--after all, there is a TON of double-crossing going on) It was interesting to see how all her classmates viewed Regina--her former best friends, the victims of her harassment, people she didn't even know. And I'm glad that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a> doesn't make Regina out to have an epiphany and complete change of character. She realizes that what she did was wrong but she also realizes that you can't just apologize and forgive and forget. I liked the analysis of right and wrong that went on in this book and especially found it realistic how quickly the tormented can become the tormentor and vice versa. It reminded me of <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanford_prison_experiment" rel="nofollow noopener">Philip Zimabardo's prison experiments at Stanford</a>.<br /><br />My first read of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a>' was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8470445.Fall_for_Anything" title="Fall for Anything by Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Fall for Anything</a> and I was totally impressed with how well she dealt with gritty issues. At times, her books feel almost painfully realistic. This one definitely gives you the feeling of what bullying actually feels like--about the hopelessness and loneliness of it all. And about how either willfully or negligently unaware parents and teachers can be. This book has one of the scariest scenes I've ever read--I'm totally serious. Don't read this spoiler unless you really want it to be spoiled or you have read the book: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The incident that leads to Regina's shunning involves Anna's boyfriend nearly raping Regina at a party. Later on in the book, they lock Regina and her assailant in a storage room together. (only two people really know what happened; everyone else believes that Donnie and Regina just slept together) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I was seriously beyond nervous and scared about what would happen. I have goosebumps just recalling the scene.<br /><br />While I can't say that this book is a pleasure to read, I'd recommend it to anyone who likes gritty YA contemporary fiction and can stomach reading about verbal and physical abuse for an entire book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16393977960758847457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_715743192" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/715743192" />
    <a title="Trudi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1416912-trudi"><img alt="Trudi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446613110p2/1416912.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/715743192?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trudi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trudi" href="/user/show/1416912-trudi">Trudi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=bullying">bullying</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=oh-canada">oh-canada</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=twss">twss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1416912-trudi?shelf=girls-behaving-badly">girls-behaving-badly</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer715743192" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5104718031386976369"><blockquote><b>Elaine:</b> (on boys giving wedgies) Boys are sick.<br/><b>Jerry:</b> What do girls do?<br/><b>Elaine:</b> We just tease someone 'til they develop an eating disorder.~<i>Seinfeld</i></blockquote> There can be something so vicious and primal about the way young women torment and bully each other. It's tribal and unrelenting and it disturbs me to my very core because I have three young nieces, one of who is on the cusp of tweendom. And right now I can't decide what would be worse - to have them grow up to be the bullies? Or the bullied? <br/><br/>All I c</span>
  <span id="freeText5104718031386976369" style="display:none"><blockquote><b>Elaine:</b> (on boys giving wedgies) Boys are sick.<br /><b>Jerry:</b> What do girls do?<br /><b>Elaine:</b> We just tease someone 'til they develop an eating disorder.~<i>Seinfeld</i></blockquote> There can be something so vicious and primal about the way young women torment and bully each other. It's tribal and unrelenting and it disturbs me to my very core because I have three young nieces, one of who is on the cusp of tweendom. And right now I can't decide what would be worse - to have them grow up to be the bullies? Or the bullied? <br /><br />All I can think of to do is to support their parents in any way I can, and stand vigilant to all warning signs and distress signals of it going either way (and pray that they will each find a neutral safety zone that falls outside the worst of the predator/prey relationships they are sure to confront). <br /><br />Meet Regina Afton. She is at the very top of her high school's food chain, orchestrating feeding frenzies and character assassinations on a whim. But all that's about to change when after a drunken party it gets out that Regina had sex with her best friend's boyfriend. It doesn't matter that this is a lie. It doesn't matter that the boyfriend in fact tried to rape Regina. All that matters is what her "friends" are willing to believe.<br /><br />Suddenly, Regina is enemy number one, being targeted as "slut" and "whore" in a ruthless, protracted campaign that only gets worse with each passing day. Summers paints a brutish portrait of the realities of bullying that left me squirming and feeling sick to my stomach. <br /><br />Point of note: this is hardcore <i>realistic fiction</i>. There are no punches pulled here. If you are sensitive in any way to teen profanity, sexual content, alcohol consumption or drug abuse, then this book is probably not for you. However, if you are seeking out a well-written, emotional, <i>honest</i> book about the dark side of bullying amongst girls, then please read this. Then after you read it, recommend it to all the young women that you know. <br /><br />For sure this book is dark. For sure there are scenes that are very difficult to read. However, as Regina fights for her survival, there is also hope and humor as she moves closer to uncovering her greatest strengths (and weaknesses). <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1487748.Courtney_Summers" title="Courtney Summers" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney Summers</a> is an author to watch.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5104718031386976369" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3619850441" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3619850441" />
    <a title="L A i N E Y" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y"><img alt="L A i N E Y" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546138360p2/10752235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3619850441?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L A i N E Y" class="user" itemprop="url" name="L A i N E Y" href="/user/show/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y">L A i N E Y</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y?shelf=psychological">psychological</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y?shelf=unforgettable">unforgettable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y?shelf=wow">wow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y?shelf=feel-this">feel-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y?shelf=marvelous-writing">marvelous-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10752235-l-a-i-n-e-y?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3619850441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5090376190552418777"><blockquote>
  <b>“If I have to live with this, I don’t want it to be hard.”</b>
</blockquote><br/>I wonder if you look up synonyms for ‘poignant’ you’d find the name Courtney Summers in there? Because it should be. <br/><br/>The ability to succinctly convey this much complex struggles, this overflowing of emotions in the span of less than 300 pages is the very definition of poignant if you ask me. What is even more stunning is that she keeps doing it book after book after book, unfailingly. With <i>such</i> ease.<br/><br/>If she was a journalist she would b</span>
  <span id="freeText5090376190552418777" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>“If I have to live with this, I don’t want it to be hard.”</b>
</blockquote><br />I wonder if you look up synonyms for ‘poignant’ you’d find the name Courtney Summers in there? Because it should be. <br /><br />The ability to succinctly convey this much complex struggles, this overflowing of emotions in the span of less than 300 pages is the very definition of poignant if you ask me. What is even more stunning is that she keeps doing it book after book after book, unfailingly. With <i>such</i> ease.<br /><br />If she was a journalist she would be one of those hard-hitting, take-no-prisoners journos who doesn’t shy away from tackling the issues head on.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“I push myself up on my elbows, my knees. Stand. Stand, Regina. It’s easy. Stand. You do it everyday.”</b>
</blockquote><br />Her characters are an acquired taste you might say. <i>She writes in-your-face heroines</i> and she unflinchingly handles girls’ issues. She makes those who love perfect snowflake characters need to avert their eyes.<br /><br />It’s a ‘mean girls’ story, yes. But not in the ordinary way. This one is complex to say the least. The perspectives, the past devastations and the repercussions from them. Not to mention the attempted <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[rapes. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[rape <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><i>sss</i> as in plural. And the mental breakdown and the overwhelming anxiety of it all. <br /><br />You truly need certain level of toughness to finish the book. That’s not a warning or anything it’s just a fact. There’re triggers left and right. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“A whole world exists outside of this hellhole.”</b>
</blockquote><br />To all Reginas, Michaels and Lizes out there - please stay strong. We are all rooting for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5090376190552418777" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_64193525" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64193525" />
    <a title="Kristi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi"><img alt="Kristi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496094866p2/1310688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64193525?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=own-arc">own-arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64193525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6090936036351334647">Three words: (some girls are) very very mean<br/><br/>I really wish I could write an intellectual, well thought out, comprehensive review, that could do an exceptional book justice. Because if a book ever deserved that type of review it would be Some Girls Are. <br/><br/>I honestly don’t know how Courtney does it. How can she write a character that is a bitch, in all essence of the word.... and make me like her.... feel sorry for her even! I should hate her, hate all that she stands for, for all those bitches in hi</span>
  <span id="freeText6090936036351334647" style="display:none">Three words: (some girls are) very very mean<br /><br />I really wish I could write an intellectual, well thought out, comprehensive review, that could do an exceptional book justice. Because if a book ever deserved that type of review it would be Some Girls Are. <br /><br />I honestly don’t know how Courtney does it. How can she write a character that is a bitch, in all essence of the word.... and make me like her.... feel sorry for her even! I should hate her, hate all that she stands for, for all those bitches in high school that thought they were.... well that’s another story for a different day. <br /><br />That’s who Regina is- a bitch, and yet, I empathized with her. I felt sorry for her. I found myself nodding in agreement, with her conniving plans to get back at the girls that were making her life a living hell. Who brainwashed me into feeling this way... Courtney Summers did, that’s who. She manipulated me with her words! She used her amazing talent to deconstruct my view of something that had always been black and white, bitch and non-bitch and made it... GRAY! How dare you!? Now I’m wondering... do bitches have feelings too....? Do bitches deserve second chances. Do bitches deserve the sweetest guy on the planet? <br /><br />Speaking of sweetest guys on the planet.... was anyone else feeling that tension between those two, or was it just me. I know it couldn’t possibly be just me... but I just wanted to scream..KISS HER ALREADY! I know you hate her, but give her a big ole’ I hate you kiss!<br /><br />I really wanted to do intellectual, but it’s obviously not happening. <br /><br />Seriously though... I can’t say enough good things about this book. Courtney has a very distinct style, and I really enjoy reading her books. She has great characterization, the plot is just insane... when you think these girls couldn’t be more mean, well they can and they Are. <br /><br />I could not put this book down, and yet.. it was hard to read. I literally picked it up hoping to get a few chapters in and ended up reading the whole thing through. <br /><br />The realistic portrayal of these girls is absolutely disturbing, in a grossly addicting way. You don’t want to see what horrible things they do next... yet you do. How is that possible... am I just a masochist like that?<br /><br />And here I raise my glass... to Courtney Summers... the queen of mean. Not that I’m saying Courtney is mean, she is in fact very sweet, but damn, she knows how to write some mean ass girls!<br /><br />I’m ready for book three, NOW. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6090936036351334647" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
